# Fault Localization: ACPI Video Backlight Control Failure

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/linux--55b2af1c (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/linux--55b2af1c (mirror of torvalds/linux)
- **Kernel Version**: 5.6.7
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: ACPI
- **Component**: Video/Backlight

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 207835
**Summary**: ACPI video backlight brightness control does not work on Acer TravelMate 5735Z by default

On the Intel GM45/GMA 4500MHD laptop with Debian Sid/unstable and Linux 5.6.7 and GNOME Shell 3.36.2, trying to change the brightness of the internal display using the function keys, GNOME shows the OSD, which seems to have five levels (from acer_wmi?), but the actual brightness does *not* change. There is only `/sys/class/backlight/intel_backlight/brightness` though, and writing values to it seems to work.

Booting the system with `acpi_backlight=vendor`, exposes `/sys/devices/platform/acer-wmi/backlight/acer-wmi/brightness`, but the behavior is the same.

Booting the system with `acpi_backlight=native` or `acpi_backlight=native`, changing the brightness with the function keys works, and there now seem to be 15 (or 16) levels.

```
$ grep '.*' /sys/class/dmi/id/*_* 2> /dev/null
/sys/class/dmi/id/bios_date:07/26/2011
/sys/class/dmi/id/bios_vendor:Acer
/sys/class/dmi/id/bios_version:V1.14
/sys/class/dmi/id/board_asset_tag:Base Board Asset Tag
/sys/class/dmi/id/board_name:BA51_MV
/sys/class/dmi/id/board_vendor:Acer
/sys/class/dmi/id/board_version:V1.14
/sys/class/dmi/id/chassis_asset_tag:
/sys/class/dmi/id/chassis_type:10
/sys/class/dmi/id/chassis_vendor:Acer
/sys/class/dmi/id/chassis_version:V1.14
/sys/class/dmi/id/product_family:Intel_Mobile
/sys/class/dmi/id/product_name:TravelMate 5735Z
/sys/class/dmi/id/product_sku:Montevina_Fab
/sys/class/dmi/id/product_version:V1.14
/sys/class/dmi/id/sys_vendor:Acer
```

## Task

You are a fault localization agent. Given the bug report above, your task is to identify the **exact source file(s)** and **function(s)/data structure(s)** in the Linux kernel source tree (at `/workspace`) that need to be modified to fix this bug.

You must:
1. Analyze the bug report to understand the symptoms and context
2. Search the kernel source code to identify the relevant subsystem and files
3. Narrow down to the specific file(s) and function(s)/data structure(s) that contain the bug or need modification
4. Write your findings to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` in the following format:

```json
{
  "buggy_files": ["path/to/file.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["function_or_struct_name"],
  "confidence": 0.8,
  "reasoning": "Brief explanation of why these locations are the fault"
}
```

**Important**: Paths should be relative to the kernel source root (e.g., `kernel/sched/core.c`, not `/workspace/kernel/sched/core.c`).

## Success Criteria

- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy file(s)
- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy function(s) or data structure(s)

60-assistanttext-
Now I have enough information. Let me create the fault localization result:

Based on my analysis:

1. **The Bug**: The Acer TravelMate 5735Z is missing from the ACPI backlight type detection table
2. **Why it's a problem**: 
   - By default, the system doesn't detect that it needs the native (intel_backlight) driver
   - The autodetect logic in `acpi_video_get_backlight_type()` returns "video" or another type
   - This causes the acer-wmi driver to disable its brightness capability (at line 2211 in acer-wmi.c)
   - The ACPI video driver can't control brightness properly either
   - But intel_backlight works fine when explicitly set with `acpi_backlight=native`

3. **The Fix Location**: The TravelMate 5735Z needs to be added to the `video_detect_dmi_table` in `drivers/acpi/video_detect.c` with the `video_detect_force_native` callback, similar to other Acer models that need native backlight support.

70-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully completed the fault localization analysis. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Fault Localization Result

**Buggy File**: `drivers/acpi/video_detect.c`

**Buggy Function/Data Structure**: `video_detect_dmi_table` array

**Confidence**: 0.95

### Analysis

The Acer TravelMate 5735Z is missing from the `video_detect_dmi_table`, which is the kernel's ACPI backlight type detection quirk table. This causes the following issue:

1. **Default Behavior**: Without a quirk entry, the autodetect logic in `acpi_video_get_backlight_type()` defaults to `acpi_backlight_video` for this system
2. **Effect on acer-wmi**: This causes the acer-wmi driver to disable its brightness capability (line 2210-2211 in acer-wmi.c) since the backlight type is not "vendor"
3. **Result**: Neither the acer-wmi driver nor the generic ACPI video driver can control brightness properly
4. **Proof**: The bug report confirms that `acpi_backlight=native` makes brightness control work perfectly with 15-16 brightness levels, proving that intel_backlight (native) is the correct driver for this model

### Solution

The TravelMate 5735Z needs to be added to the `video_detect_dmi_table` with the `video_detect_force_native` callback (similar to existing entries for models like Dell Vostro V131 and Lenovo Ideapad S405), so the system uses intel_backlight by default instead of trying to use acer-wmi or the generic ACPI video driver.

The fault localization result has been written to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`.

    "drivers/acpi/video_detect.c"

  "buggy_functions": [

  ],
  "confidence": 0.95,
  "reasoning": "The Acer TravelMate 5735Z is missing from the video_detect_dmi_table. This causes the ACPI backlight type detection logic to not recognize that this system needs to use the native (intel_backlight) driver. By default, the autodetect logic returns acpi_backlight_video or another non-native type, which causes the acer-wmi driver to disable its brightness capability (via acpi_video_get_backlight_type() check at line 2210 in acer-wmi.c), and the ACPI video driver fails to control brightness. However, the bug report confirms that intel_backlight works perfectly when explicitly set with acpi_backlight=native, proving that this model needs a force_native quirk entry in video_detect_dmi_table to work properly by default."
